Statistics

Problem Statement for "Chains5"

Problem Statement

All problems in this problem set are about "chains": collections of nested ranges of integers. All problems are independent, but use the same definitions. Each problem statement contains the definitions it needs. If a term appears in multiple problems, the definition is always identical.

Definitions follow. The defined term is always in uppercase.

  • An INTERVAL [x,y) with x &lt;= y is the set of integers that are greater than or equal to x, and strictly less than y.
  • There is only one EMPTY INTERVAL but it has multiple equivalent notations. For example, [0,0) and [3,3) both denote the empty interval. Note that [3,0) is not a valid interval, because an interval [x,y) must have x &lt;= y.
  • An interval I1 is called a PROPER SUBSET of an interval I2 if I2 contains all elements of I1 and at least one other element.
  • A CHAIN is a nonempty sequence of intervals such that each interval (except for the last one) is a proper subset of the next interval.

You are given a collection of intervals. Use them to build a collection of valid chains. Minimize the number of chains. Return that minimal number of chains.

The first few intervals are given in the int[]s x and y: for each valid i, you have an interval [ x[i], y[i] ).

The remaining intervals will be generated pseudorandomly as follows: 

while you have fewer than n intervals in your collection:
    seed = (a * seed + b) mod c
    newx = seed mod m
    seed = (a * seed + b) mod c
    newy = seed mod m
    if newx &gt; newy:
        swap( newx, newy )
    add the interval [newx, newy) to your collection

Definition

Class:
Chains5
Method:
construct
Parameters:
int[], int[], int, int, int, int, int, int
Returns:
int
Method signature:
int construct(int[] x, int[] y, int n, int seed, int a, int b, int c, int m)
(be sure your method is public)

Notes

  • The collection may contain multiple copies of the same interval. In that case, exactly that many copies of that interval must appear in the collection of chains you'll construct.
  • The reference solution works for any input of the given size, it does not depend on any properties of the pseudorandom generator.
  • Watch out for integer overflow when generating your input.

Constraints

  • g will be between 0 and 200, inclusive.
  • Each of x and y will have exactly g elements.
  • For each valid i, 0 <= x[i] <= y[i] < 2^30.
  • n will be between g and 100,000, inclusive.
  • c will be between 1 and 2^30, inclusive.
  • m will be between 1 and c, inclusive.
  • seed, a, and b will be between 0 and c-1, inclusive.

Examples

  1. {1, 2, 1}

    {7, 4, 10}

    3

    0

    0

    0

    1

    1

    Returns: 1

    We can form one chain using all three intervals: [2,4), [1,7), [1,10).

    1

    1

    Returns: 2

    We need two separate chains, each consisting of a single interval.
